25:T2bb5,<entryFree id="n20250" key="سَكَنَ" type="main">     
                  <form>       
                     <itype>1</itype>        
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">سَكَنَ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form>, (S, Mgh, L, Msb, K,) aor.      
    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Bu" lang="ar">سَكُنَ</orth>
                  </form>, (L,) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">سُكُونٌ</foreign>, (S, Mgh, L, Msb, K,) said of a thing, (S, L,) of a thing that moves, (Mgh, Msb,) <hi rend="ital">It was,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">became, still, motionless, stationary, in a state of rest, quiet, calm,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">unruffled,</hi> (<foreign lang="ar">هَدَأَ</foreign>, Abu-l-'Abbás, L, or <foreign lang="ar">قَرَّ</foreign>, K,) <hi rend="ital">after motion;</hi> (Abu-l-'Abbás, L;) <hi rend="ital">its motion</hi> [<hi rend="ital">ceased,</hi> or] <hi rend="ital">went away;</hi> (L, Msb;) and in like manner said of a man, and of a beast: (Abu-l-'Abbás, L:) and said of anything such as wind and heat and cold and the like; of rain; [and of pain;] and of anger; [&amp;c.;] <hi rend="ital">it was,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">became, still, calm, tranquillized, appeased, allayed, assuaged,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">quelled;</hi> [<hi rend="ital">it died away, passed away,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">ceased to be:</hi> and <hi rend="ital">it remitted,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">subsided; became alleviated, light, slight,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">gentle:</hi>] and said of a man [or beast or the like, and of a voice or sound], <hi rend="ital">he</hi> [or <hi rend="ital">it</hi>] <hi rend="ital">was,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">became, still,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">silent.</hi> (L.) [Hence,] one says, <foreign lang="ar">سَكَنَ الدَّمْعُ</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">الدَّمُ</foreign>, meaning <foreign lang="ar">رَقَأَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">The tears,</hi> and <hi rend="ital">the blood, stopped,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">ceased to flow</hi>]. (S and Mgh in art. <foreign lang="ar">رقاٌ</foreign>.) [And one says of heat, and cold, and pain, &amp;c., <foreign lang="ar">سَكَنَ عَنْهُ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">It passed away from him; quitted him.</hi> And <foreign lang="ar">سَكَنَتِ النَّارُ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">The fire became extinguished;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">became allayed</hi> or <hi rend="ital">assuaged; subsided;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">ceased to flame</hi> or <hi rend="ital">blaze</hi> or <hi rend="ital">burn fiercely,</hi>]          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  [Hence also, <hi rend="ital">It</hi> (a letter) <hi rend="ital">was</hi> or <hi rend="ital">became, quiescent;</hi> i. e., <hi rend="ital">without a vowel immediately following it; contr. of</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">تَحَرَّكَ</foreign>.]          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  And <foreign lang="ar">سَكَنَ إِلَيْهِ</foreign>, (Msb, [where the aor. is said to be      
    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Bi" lang="ar">سَكِنَ</orth>
                  </form>, but this is either a mistake or rare, for the aor. accord. to common usage is      
    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Bu" lang="ar">سَكُنَ</orth>
                  </form>, as in the Kur vii.] 189 and xxx. 20,]) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">سُكُونٌ</foreign> (Mgh, Msb) and <foreign lang="ar">سَكَنٌ</foreign>, (Msb,) <hi rend="ital">He trusted to it,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">relied upon it, so as to be,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">become, easy,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">quiet, in mind; i. q.</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">رَكَنَ إِلَيْهِ</foreign>; (S and K &amp;c. in art. <foreign lang="ar">ركن</foreign>;) and <pb n="1393"/> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">اِطْمَأَنَّ إِلَيْهِ</foreign>; (TA in art. <foreign lang="ar">طمن</foreign>;) [and <foreign lang="ar">اِعْتَمَدَ عَلَيْهِ</foreign>; and <foreign lang="ar">وَثِقَ بِهِ</foreign>; &amp;c.; and <hi rend="ital">he inclined to it;</hi> syn. <foreign lang="ar">مَالَ إِلَيْهِ</foreign>; and <hi rend="ital">became familiar with it;</hi> syn. <foreign lang="ar">اِسُتَأْنَسَ بِهِ</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">أَلِفَ</foreign>; agreeably with explanations here following;] namely, a thing: (Msb:) and <foreign lang="ar">سَكَنَ إِلَيْهَا</foreign>, aor.      
    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Bu" lang="ar">سَكُنَ</orth>
                  </form>, <hi rend="ital">he trusted to her,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">relied upon her, so as to be,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">become, easy,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">quiet, in mind;</hi> &amp;c., as above; syn. <foreign lang="ar">اِطْمَأَنَّ إِلَيْهَا</foreign>; (Ksh and Bd in vii. 189, and Ksh in xxx. 20;) and <foreign lang="ar">مَالَ إِلَيْهَا</foreign>; (Ksh in vii. 189, and the same and Bd in xxx. 20;) and <foreign lang="ar">اِسْتَأْنَسَ بِهَا</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">أَلِفَ</foreign>; (Bd in the same two places;) namely, his wife. (Ksh and Bd.)          <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  And <foreign lang="ar">سَكَنَ الَّدارَ</foreign>, (S, MA, Mgh, L, Msb, K,) and <foreign lang="ar">فِى الدَّارِ</foreign>, (Mgh, Msb,) and <foreign lang="ar">بِالمَكَانِ</foreign>, (L,) aor.      
    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Bu" lang="ar">سَكُنَ</orth>
                  </form>, (L, Msb, JM,) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">سُكْنَى</foreign> (MA, Mgh, L, JM) and <foreign lang="ar">سُكُونٌ</foreign> (MA, L) and <foreign lang="ar">سُكْنٌ</foreign>, (MA,) or   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n20250-1" target="سُكْنَى" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n20263"/></foreign> is a simple subst., and the inf. n. is <foreign lang="ar">سكن</foreign>, (Msb, [accord. to which the latter is app. <foreign lang="ar">سَكَنٌ</foreign>, for it is there said that the verb in this case is like <foreign lang="ar">طَلَبَ</foreign>, the unaugmented inf. n. of which is <foreign lang="ar">طَلَبٌ</foreign>, but this inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">سَكَنُ</foreign> I have not found elsewhere, and what is generally used as the inf. n. or quasi-inf. n. of the verb in this case is   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n20250-2" target="سُكْنَى" n="2" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n20263"/></foreign>,]) or   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n20250-3" target="سُكْنَى" n="3" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n20263"/></foreign> is a subst. in the sense of <foreign lang="ar">إِسْكَانٌ</foreign>, as expl. below, (Mgh,) [or rather it is also a subst. in this sense,] <hi rend="ital">He inhabited,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">dwelt</hi> or <hi rend="ital">abode in, the house</hi> [and <hi rend="ital">the place</hi>]. (MA, Mgh.) <foreign lang="ar">وَلَهُ مَا سَكَنَ فِى ٱللَّيْلِ وَٱلنَّهَارِ</foreign>, in the Kur [vi. 13], is from <foreign lang="ar">السُّكْنَى</foreign> (Ksh, Bd) or from <foreign lang="ar">السُّكُونُ</foreign>: (Bd:) if from the former, (Ksh, Bd,) it signifies <hi rend="ital">To Him belongeth what taketh up its abode in the night and the day;</hi> (IAar, Ksh, * Bd, * L, Jel;) meaning, what the night and the day include within their limits: (Ksh, * Bd:) or, if from <foreign lang="ar">السُّكُونُ</foreign>, (Bd,) <hi rend="ital">what is still,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">motionless,</hi> (Abu-l-'Abbás, Bd, L,) and what moves; one of the two contraries being mentioned as sufficient [to show what is intended] without the other; (Bd;) app. meaning the creation, collectively, or all created beings. (Abu-l-'Abbás, L.)          <sense type="b" n="5">-b5-</sense>  And <foreign lang="ar">سَكَنَ</foreign>, (L, K,) aor.      
    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Bu" lang="ar">سَكُنَ</orth>
                  </form>, (K,) <hi rend="ital">He became such as is termed</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">مِسْكِين</foreign> [q. v.]; (L, K;) as also <foreign lang="ar">سَكُنَ</foreign>, (K,) and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n20250-4" target="اسكن" n="4" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n20253"/></foreign>, and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n20250-5" target="تسكّن" n="5" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n20254"/></foreign>, and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n20250-6" target="تَمَسْكَنَ" n="6" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n20256"/></foreign>: (L, K:) and [thus it means particularly] <hi rend="ital">he was,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">became, lowly, humble,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">submissive;</hi> and <hi rend="ital">low, abject, abased, and weak;</hi> as also

And it is said in a trad., respecting the Prophet, on the occasion of the coming down of revelation, <foreign lang="ar">فَغَشِيَتْهُ السَّكِينَةُ</foreign>, meaning <hi rend="ital">And calmness,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">tranquillity, and</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">غَيْبَة</foreign> [i. e., as here used, <hi rend="ital">absence of mind from self and others by its being exclusively occupied by the contemplation of divine things</hi>], <hi rend="ital">came upon him.</hi> (L.) And in the Kur [ii. 249], it is said, [with reference to the coming of the ark of the covenant,] <foreign lang="ar">فِيهِ سَكِينَةٌ مِنْ رَبِّكُمْ</foreign>, meaning [<hi rend="ital">In which shall be</hi>] <hi rend="ital">a cause of your becoming tranquil,</hi> [or <hi rend="ital">easy in your minds,</hi>] when it cometh to you [<hi rend="ital">from your Lord</hi>]: (Zj, L, K:) or, as some say, there was in it <hi rend="ital">a head like that of the cat; when it uttered a cry, victory betided the Children of Israel:</hi> (L:) or <hi rend="ital">a thing having a head like that of the cat</hi> [<hi rend="ital">and a tail like that of the cat</hi> (Bd)], <hi rend="ital">of chrysolite and sapphire, and a pair of wings:</hi> (L, K:) or <hi rend="ital">an image like the cat,</hi> that was with them among their forces, <hi rend="ital">on the appearance of which their enemies were routed:</hi> or <hi rend="ital">an animal having a face like that of a human being, compact</hi> [<hi rend="ital">in substance</hi>], <hi rend="ital">the rest thereof being unsubstantial like the wind and the air:</hi> or <hi rend="ital">the images of the Prophets, from Adam to Mohammad:</hi> (Bd:) or <hi rend="ital">the signs,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">miracles, with the performance of which Moses was endowed, and to which they trusted so as to be easy,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">quiet, in their minds:</hi> (L:) or by the <foreign lang="ar">تَابُوت</foreign> to which these words refer is meant the heart, [or rather the chest, i. e. bosom,] and the <foreign lang="ar">سكينة</foreign> is the <hi rend="ital">knowledge, and purity,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">sincerity, in the heart</hi> [or <hi rend="ital">bosom</hi>]. (Bd.)                   <form>       
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">مِسْكِينٌ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form> (S, Mgh, L, Msb, K, &amp;c.) and <foreign lang="ar">مَسْكِينٌ</foreign>, (L, Msb, K,) the latter anomalous, for there is no [other] instance of the measure <foreign lang="ar">مَفْعِيلٌ</foreign>, (L,) of the dial. of Benoo-Asad, (L, Msb,) mentioned by Ks as heard by him from some one or more of that tribe, (L,) others saying <foreign lang="ar">مِسْكِينٌ</foreign>, (Msb,) of the measure <foreign lang="ar">مِفْعِيلٌ</foreign> (L) from <foreign lang="ar">السُّكُونُ</foreign>, because the person to whom it is applied trusts to, or relies upon, others, so as to be, or become, easy, or quiet, in mind: (Mgh, L, Msb:) primarily, (L,) it signifies <hi rend="ital">Lowly, humble,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">submissive;</hi> (IAth, Mgh, L;) and therefore the Prophet said, <foreign lang="ar">اَللّٰهُمَّ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">أَحْيِنِى مِسْكِينًا وَأَمِتْنِى مِسْكِينًا وَاْحْشُرْنِى فِى زُمْرَةِ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">المَسَاكِينِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">O God, make me to live lowly, and make me to die lowly, and gather me among the congregation of the lowly</hi>]: (Mgh, * L:) and hence it sometimes applies to him who possesses little and [sometimes] to him who possesses much: (L:) sometimes, (S,) it signifies (S, IAth, L, Msb, K) also (IAth, L) <hi rend="ital">low, abject, ignominious,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">in a state of abasement</hi> or <hi rend="ital">humiliation;</hi> (S, IAth, L, Msb, K;) and <hi rend="ital">weak;</hi> (S, L, K;) and <hi rend="ital">subdued,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">oppressed;</hi> though possessing riches or competence: (Msb:) [therefore] Sb says, it is one of the words expressive of pity, or compassion; [and as such may be rendered <hi rend="ital">poor;</hi>] you say, <foreign lang="ar">مَرَرْت بِهِ المِسْكِينَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">I passed by him,</hi> I mean <hi rend="ital">the poor</hi> man], putting it in the accus. case by the implication of <foreign lang="ar">أَعْنِى</foreign>, though it may be in the genitive case as a substitute [for the pronoun], and in the nom. case by the suppression of <foreign lang="ar">هُوَ</foreign> meant to be understood: (L:) in other cases, (S,) it is <hi rend="ital">syn. with</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">فَقِيرٌ</foreign>, (S, L, Msb,) meaning (Msb) <hi rend="ital">destitute,</hi> i. e. <hi rend="ital">possessing nothing:</hi> (L, Msb, K:) or accord. to ISk, <foreign lang="ar">مسكين</foreign> means thus; but the <foreign lang="ar">فقير</foreign> is he who possesses a sufficiency of the means of subsistence: (Msb:) or the former means <hi rend="ital">possessing somewhat;</hi> (L;) or [rather] <hi rend="ital">needy,</hi> i. e. <hi rend="ital">possessing what is not sufficient</hi> (L, K) <hi rend="ital">for him</hi> (K) or <hi rend="ital">for his family:</hi> (L:) or <hi rend="ital">caused by poverty to have little power of motion;</hi> (L, K;) thus expl. by Aboo-Is-hák; but this is improbable; for <foreign lang="ar">مسكين</foreign> has the meaning of an active part. n., and his explanation [like one of the others mentioned above] makes it to have that of a pass. part. n.: (L:) Yoo says the like of ISk: (Msb:) he used to say that the <foreign lang="ar">مسكين</foreign> is in a harder condition than the <foreign lang="ar">فقير</foreign>: (S, L, * Msb: *) he says, I asked an Arab of the desert, Art thou <foreign lang="ar">فقير</foreign>? and he answered, No, by God, but rather <foreign lang="ar">مسكين</foreign>; (S, L, * Msb;) but 'Alee Ibn-Hamzeh says that this man may have meant that he was low, or abject, by reason of his distance from his people and his home; and that he does not think he meant anything but that: (L:) [J also adds,] it is said in a trad. that the <foreign lang="ar">مسكين</foreign> is not he whom a mouthful or two mouthfuls will turn back, or away, but is only he who does not beg, and who is not known so that he may be given [anything]; (S;) but Ziyádet-Allah Ibn-Ahmad says that the <foreign lang="ar">فقير</foreign> is he who sits in his house, not begging, and the <foreign lang="ar">مسكين</foreign> is he who begs and is given; and hence it is argued that the latter is in a better condition than the former; though it indicates that the former is more highminded than the latter: (L:) accord. to As, the <foreign lang="ar">مسكين</foreign> is better in condition than the <foreign lang="ar">فقير</foreign>; and this is [said to be] the right assertion, (Mgh, L, Msb,) for the pl. of the former is applied in the Kur xviii. 78 to men possessing a ship, or boat, which is worth a considerable sum; (L, Msb;) but they may have been thus termed because they were humbled and abased by the tyranny of the king who took every ship, or boat, that he found upon the sea, by force; (L;) and it is said that these men were hirers, not owners, of the vessel: (TA voce <foreign lang="ar">فَقِيرٌ</foreign>, q. v.:) 'Alee Ibn-Hamzeh says, that the <foreign lang="ar">مسكين</foreign> is better in condition than the <foreign lang="ar">فقير</foreign> is shown by a passage in the Kur [ix. 60], where it is said that the poor-rates are for the <foreign lang="ar">فُقَرَآء</foreign> and the <foreign lang="ar">مَسَاكِين</foreign>; for you will find the classes to be there mentioned in such an order that the second is better in condition than the first, and the third than the second, and in like manner the fourth and the fifth and the sixth and the seventh and the eighth: and he says that the same is shown by the fact that the Arabs sometimes used <foreign lang="ar">مسكين</foreign> as a proper name, but not <foreign lang="ar">فقير</foreign>: (L:) or when these two words are used together, they differ in signification; and when used separately, they [sometimes] signify the same: (El-Bedr El-Karáfee, TA in art. <foreign lang="ar">فقر</foreign>:) [see more voce <foreign lang="ar">فَقِيرٌ</foreign>:] a woman is termed <foreign lang="ar">مِسْكِينَةٌ</foreign> (Sb, S, L, Msb, K) and <foreign lang="ar">مِسْكِينٌ</foreign> also; (S, L, K;) the former by way of assimilation to <foreign lang="ar">فَقِيرَةٌ</foreign>; (Sb, S, L;) the latter being accord. to rule, for an epithet of the measure <foreign lang="ar">مِفْعِيلٌ</foreign> is regularly applied alike to a male and a female; (S, Msb;) or, as Abu-l-Hasan says, this is only when it is an intensive epithet, which <foreign lang="ar">مِسْكِينَةٌ</foreign> is not: (L:) the pl. is <foreign lang="ar">مَسَاكِينُ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">مِسْكِينُونَ</foreign>, (S, L, K,) applied to men, (K,) or to a company of people, (S, L,) and <foreign lang="ar">مِسْكِينَاتٌ</foreign> applied to female.
